1. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, & MEDICALTREATMENT:| voluntarily consent to (and consent on behalf of any child born to

physicians, including their assistants or designees. In the case of diagnostic studies, |consent to the interpretation of the studies at an off-site
location through the use of telehealth. |consent to medical, nursing, allied health and other students observing and participating in my care
under the supervision of a qualified professional. | consent to photographic recordings or reproducible images during the surgical, medical,
and/or diagnostic procedure(s) and their use for identification, scientific, educational, or research purposes. | also consent to testing for
communicable and blood-borne infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), if a provider
orders testing for diagnostic purposes or ifthere has been an exposure to healthcare personnel. | have been given no guarantees about the
results that may be obtained from my care.
INPATIENT AND OUTPATIENT CONDITIONS AND CONSENTS
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered
nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced
practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing
treatment to patients in the Hospital are not employed by the Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or
the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established bythe
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION: | authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use
and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures
include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’
compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any
other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of
services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for mytransport to or from the Hospital;
(b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me
after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to which the patient may be
transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to
providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other
persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing
information related to drug-related conditions, alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne
infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or
its review organization paying for mycare to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | also authorize the release of my
social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.

FINDINGS:
Vertebral body height and alignment are intact. Modic type changes are present at the C3/4 level. Marrow signal
otherwise unremarkable throughout. Cervical spinal cord demonstrates no mass, edema, or syrinx. The posterior elements are intact. The prevertebral soft tissues are within normal limits. Cervical medullary junction and visualized portions of posterior fossa
are unremarkable. C2/3: Unremarkable. C3/4: Disc osteophyte complex and small central posterior disc
protrusion. Moderate central canal stenosis. Effacement of the ventral
thecal sac. There is mild right-sided neural foraminal stenosis. C4/5: Unremarkable. C5/6: Unremarkable. C6/7: Unremarkable. C7/T1: Unremarkable.
Impression:
1. Degenerative disc disease and small superimposed disc protrusion at
C3/4 causing moderate central canal and mild right-sided neural
foraminal stenosis. 2. Otherwise unremarkable exam. This report was finalized on 6/22/2019 11:50 AM by Dr. Kevin J Croce, MD.

INPATIENT AND OUTPATIENT CONDITIONS AND CONSENTS
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered
nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced
practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing
treatment to patients in the Hospital are not employed by the Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or
the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established bythe
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION: | authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use
and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures
include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’
compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any
other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of
services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for mytransport to or from the Hospital;
(b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me
after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to which the patient may be
transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to
providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other
persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing
information related to drug-related conditions, alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne
infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or
its review organization paying for mycare to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | also authorize the release of my
social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.

PREVENTING SURGICAL SITE INFECTIONS (continued) · Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination
It is important to seek emergency care right away if you have further stroke symptoms. If you get
emergency help quickly, the powerful clot-dissolving medicines can reduce the disabilities caused by a
stroke. 
For more information:
American Stroke Association
1-888-4-STROKE
www.strokeassociation.org

Why is smoking bad for me?

smoke, STOP!

diagnostic studies, | consent to the interpretation ofthe studies at anoff-site location through the use oftelehealth. |consent to
medical, nursing, allied health and other students observing and participating inmy care under the supervision of a qualified
professional. | consent to photographic recordings or reproducible images during the surgical, medical, and/or diagnostic
procedure(s) and their use for identification, scientific, educational, or research purposes. | also consent to testing for
communicable and blood-borne infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus
(HIV), ifa provider orders testing for diagnostic purposes or ifthere has been an exposure to healthcare personnel. | have
been given noguarantees about the results that may be obtained from my care.
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE
HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the
hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse
practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing treatment to patients in the Hospital are
not employed bythe Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or the Hospital bill you
receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established by the
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION:| authorize the Hospital and the health care
providers onits medical staff to use and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare
operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person,
company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’ compensation carriers, myemployer, the Medicare and
Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any other payor or itsreview organization or
third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of services provided to me on
an inpatient oroutpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for my transport to or from the Hospital; (b) any
health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may beproviding follow-up
care to me after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to
which the patient may be transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or
maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization
reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other persons or entities described inthe Hospital’s Notice of Privacy
Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing information related to drug-related conditions,
alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne infectious diseases, such as
hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or its review
organization paying for my care to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes.| also authorize the release
of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device
Tracking Act.

PREVENTING SURGICAL SITE INFECTIONS
· Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination
It is important to seek emergency care right away if you have further stroke symptoms. If you get
emergency help quickly, the powerful clot-dissolving medicines can reduce the disabilities caused by a
stroke. 
For more information:
American Stroke Association
1-888-4-STROKE
www.strokeassociation.org
IF YOU SMOKE OR USE TOBACCO PLEASE READ THE FOLLOWING:
Why is smoking bad for me?
Smoking increases the risk of heart disease, lung disease, vascular disease, stroke, and cancer. If you
smoke, STOP!

1. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, & MEDICALTREATMENT:| voluntarily consent to (and consent on behalf of any child born to
me while hospitalized) care involving routine diagnostic tests, procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my admitting and treating
physicians, including their assistants or designees. In the case of diagnostic studies, |consent to the interpretation of the studies at an off-site
location through the use of telehealth. |consent to medical, nursing, allied health and other students observing and participating in my care
under the supervision of a qualified professional. | consent to photographic recordings or reproducible images during the surgical, medical,
and/or diagnostic procedure(s) and their use for identification, scientific, educational, or research purposes. | also consent to testing for
communicable and blood-borne infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), if a provider
orders testing for diagnostic purposes or ifthere has been an exposure to healthcare personnel. | have been given no guarantees about the
results that may be obtained from my care.
INPATIENT AND OUTPATIENT CONDITIONS AND CONSENTS
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered
nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced
practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing
treatment to patients in the Hospital are not employed by the Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or
the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established bythe
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION: | authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use
and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures
include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’
compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any
other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of
services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for mytransport to or from the Hospital;
(b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me
after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to which the patient may be
transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to
providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other
persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing
information related to drug-related conditions, alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne
infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or
its review organization paying for mycare to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | also authorize the release of my
social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.
4. FINANCIAL AGREEMENT ANDASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS: |agree that | am responsible for payment of my Hospital bill. Payment of any
portion of my bill not covered by a third party payor is due upon discharge from the Hospital unless the Hospital has agreed to other
arrangements. | agree to the assignment of all third party payor benefits to the Hospital and to any health care provider rendering services to
me. |agree to pay the Hospital and other health care providers for all charges for services that are notcovered or paid by any third party
payor regardless of the reason, including but not limited to a determination by any third party payor that such services are not covered
services or medically necessary. To the extent | am a Medicare or Medicaid beneficiary, | certify that any information | provide in applying for
payment under Title XVIII (Medicare) or Title XIX (Medicaid) ofthe Social Security Act is correct. | request payment of authorized benefits to be
made on mybehalf to Baptist Health facility or to any health care provider rendering services to meby the Medicare or Medicaid program. |
hereby irrevocably appoint Hospital as my authorized representative to pursue any claims, penalties, and administrative and/or legal
remedies on my behalf for collection against any responsible payer, employer-sponsored medical benefit plans, third party liability carrier or,

regulations, | acknowledge that | am responsible for any drugs furnished to mewhile an outpatient that meet Medicare’s definition of a

Medicare requires Hospital to bill Medicare patients or other third party payers for these drugs. Medicare Part D beneficiaries may submit a
paper claim to the Medicare Part D Plan for possible reimbursement of these drugs in accordance with Medicare Drug Plan enrollment
materials.

PREVENTING SURGICAL SITE INFECTIONS
· Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination

1. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, & MEDICALTREATMENT:| voluntarily consent to (and consent on behalf of any child born to
me while hospitalized) care involving routine diagnostic tests, procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my admitting and treating
physicians, including their assistants or designees. In the case of diagnostic studies, |consent to the interpretation of the studies at an off-site
location through the use of telehealth. |consent to medical, nursing, allied health and other students observing and participating in my care
under the supervision of a qualified professional. | consent to photographic recordings or reproducible images during the surgical, medical,
and/or diagnostic procedure(s) and their use for identification, scientific, educational, or research purposes. | also consent to testing for
communicable and blood-borne infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), if a provider
orders testing for diagnostic purposes or ifthere has been an exposure to healthcare personnel. | have been given no guarantees about the
results that may be obtained from my care.
INPATIENT AND OUTPATIENT CONDITIONS AND CONSENTS
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered
nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced
practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing
treatment to patients in the Hospital are not employed by the Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or
the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established bythe
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION: | authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use
and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures
include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’
compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any
other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of
services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for mytransport to or from the Hospital;
(b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me
after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to which the patient may be
transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to
providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other
persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing
information related to drug-related conditions, alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne
infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or
its review organization paying for mycare to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | also authorize the release of my
social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.

Patient Instructions
None · Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination
It is important to seek emergency care right away if you have further stroke symptoms. If you get
emergency help quickly, the powerful clot-dissolving medicines can reduce the disabilities caused by a
stroke.

Instructions for After Discharge
Patient Instructions
None · Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination
It is important to seek emergency care right away if you have further stroke symptoms. If you get
emergency help quickly, the powerful clot-dissolving medicines can reduce the disabilities caused by a
stroke. 
For more information:
American Stroke Association
1-888-4-STROKE
www.strokeassociation.org

394545 ADMIT DATE:042619 Welcome tBaptist Health 0
Our mission is to provide you with high quality individualized care that is safe and effective to meet your
healthcare needs. We will provide you with education and instruction to help with your pain
management/recovery, and we will strive for this to be a successful process. This needs to be a team effort to
include not only your care providers at the hospital, butyou, the patient.
Our care goals are:
e To work together in providing your treatment in a respectful manner.
e To help you meet the goals of your treatment plan.
e To maintain a safe environment for the delivery of health care services at our hospital.
e To protect the safety and well-being of all patients, visitors, staff and care providers.
We value you as a patient and want to continue to provide you with high quality safe care and service. To do so,
we need to outline the expectations that will foster an effective provider- patient relationship.
The following expectations are required to maintain an effective provider- patient relationship.
Patient Behavior Expectations
e |will comply with the medical treatment plan and recommendations developed between my provider
and me.
e |will treat my care providers with dignity and respect, and |expect to be treated with dignity and respect.
e |understand that profanity, physical or verbal abuse, or any other form of violence against anyone will
not be allowed or tolerated.
e |understand that unauthorized and/or illegal drugs are not allowed in the hospital.
e For my safety, |will not leave the nursing unit where | am a patient during my treatment unless
accompanied by hospital personnel for diagnostic procedures or treatments.
e If |leave the unit, itwill be considered going against medical advice and | may be discharged from the
hospital. For any future medical care, |would need to consult my primary care MD/Provider or go to an
Emergency Room for further evaluation. Hospital staff have theright notto re-admit me for further care
unless an emergency situation exists.

INPATIENT AND OUTPATIENT CONDITIONS AND CONSENTS 91058394545 ADMIT DATE:042619
1. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, & MEDICALTREATMENT:| voluntarily consent to (and consent on behalf of any child born to
me while hospitalized) care involving routine diagnostic tests, procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my admitting and treating
physicians, including their assistants or designees. In the case of diagnostic studies, |consent to the interpretation of the studies at an off-site
location through the use of telehealth. |consent to medical, nursing, allied health and other students observing and participating in my care
under the supervision of a qualified professional. | consent to photographic recordings or reproducible images during the surgical, medical,
and/or diagnostic procedure(s) and their use for identification, scientific, educational, or research purposes. | also consent to testing for
communicable and blood-borne infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), if a provider
orders testing for diagnostic purposes or ifthere has been an exposure to healthcare personnel. | have been given no guarantees about the
results that may be obtained from my care.
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered
nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced
practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing
treatment to patients in the Hospital are not employed by the Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or
the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established bythe
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION: | authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use
and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures
include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’
compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any
other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of
services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for mytransport to or from the Hospital;
(b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me
after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to which the patient may be
transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to
providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other
persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing
information related to drug-related conditions, alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne
infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or
its review organization paying for mycare to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | also authorize the release of my
social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.
4. FINANCIAL AGREEMENT ANDASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS: |agree that | am responsible for payment of my Hospital bill. Payment of any
portion of my bill not covered by a third party payor is due upon discharge from the Hospital unless the Hospital has agreed to other
arrangements. | agree to the assignment of all third party payor benefits to the Hospital and to any health care provider rendering services to
me. |agree to pay the Hospital and other health care providers for all charges for services that are notcovered or paid by any third party
payor regardless of the reason, including but not limited to a determination by any third party payor that such services are not covered
services or medically necessary. To the extent | am a Medicare or Medicaid beneficiary, | certify that any information | provide in applying for
payment under Title XVIII (Medicare) or Title XIX (Medicaid) ofthe Social Security Act is correct. | request payment of authorized benefits to be
made on mybehalf to Baptist Health facility or to any health care provider rendering services to meby the Medicare or Medicaid program. |
hereby irrevocably appoint Hospital as my authorized representative to pursue any claims, penalties, and administrative and/or legal
remedies on my behalf for collection against any responsible payer, employer-sponsored medical benefit plans, third party liability carrier or,
any other responsible third party for any and all benefits due me for the payment of charges associated with mytreatment. This assignment
shall not be construed as an obligation of the Hospital to pursue any such right of recovery. | agree to take all actions necessary to assist
Hospital in collecting payment from any such third party payer. |understand that after reasonable notice, any unpaid account may be turned
over to a collection agency and/or attorney for collection. Should itbe necessary for the Hospital to pursue collection, | agree to pay all
reasonable collection costs, including

5. OUTPATIENT MEDICARE PATIENTS: Medicare does not cover prescription drugs with only a few exceptions. According to Medicare
regulations, | acknowledge that | am responsible for any drugs furnished to mewhile an outpatient that meet Medicare’s definition of a

Medicare requires Hospital to bill Medicare patients or other third party payers for these drugs. Medicare Part D beneficiaries may submit a
paper claim to the Medicare Part D Plan for possible reimbursement of these drugs in accordance with Medicare Drug Plan enrollment
materials.

More Information
Muscle Strain
A muscle strain is an injury that happens when a muscle is stretched longer than normal. This can happen during a fall, 
sports, or lifting. This can tear some muscle fibers. Usually, recovery from muscle strain takes 1–2 weeks. Complete
healing normally takes 5–6 weeks. This condition is first treated with PRICE therapy. This involves: · Protecting your muscle from being injured again. · Resting your injured muscle. · Icing your injured muscle. · Applying pressure (compression) to your injured muscle. This may be done with a splint or elastic bandage. · Raising (elevating) your injured muscle.
Your doctor may also recommend medicine for pain.
Follow these instructions at home:
If you have a splint: · Wear the splint as told by your doctor. Take it off only as told by your doctor. · Loosen the splint if your fingers or toes tingle, get numb, or turn cold and blue. · Keep the splint clean. · If the splint is not waterproof:
○ Do not let it get wet.
○ Cover it with a watertight covering when you take a bath or a shower.
Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling
· If directed, put ice on your injured area.
○ If you have a removable splint, take it off as told by your doctor.
○ Put ice in a plastic bag.
○ Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
○ Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day. · Move your fingers or toes often. This helps to avoid stiffness and lessen swelling. · Raise your injured area above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down.

More Information (continued)
·
· Wear an elastic bandage as told by your doctor. Make sure it is not too tight.
General instructions · Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor. · Limit your activity. Rest your injured muscle as told by your doctor. Your doctor may say that gentle 
movements are okay. · If physical therapy was prescribed, do exercises as told by your doctor. · Do not put pressure on any part of the splint until it is fully hardened. This may take many hours. · Do not use any products that contain nicotine or tobacco, such as cigarettes and e-cigarettes. These can delay 
bone healing. If you need help quitting, ask your doctor. · Warm up before you exercise. This helps to prevent more muscle strains. · Ask your doctor when it is safe to drive if you have a splint. · Keep all follow-up visits as told by your doctor. This is important.
Contact a doctor if: · You have more pain or swelling in your injured area.
Get help right away if: · You have any of these problems in your injured area:
○ You have numbness.
○ You have tingling.
○ You lose a lot of strength.
Summary
· A muscle strain is an injury that happens when a muscle is stretched longer than normal. · This condition is first treated with PRICE therapy. This includes protecting, resting, icing, adding pressure, and 
raising your injury. · Limit your activity. Rest your injured muscle as told by your doctor. Your doctor may say that gentle 
movements are okay. · Warm up before you exercise. This helps to prevent more muscle strains.

any questions you have with your health care provider.
Document Released: [DOB-809] Document Revised: [DOB-810] Document Reviewed: [DOB-811]
Elsevier Interactive Patient Education © 2019 Elsevier Inc. · Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination
It is important to seek emergency care right away if you have further stroke symptoms. If you get
emergency help quickly, the powerful clot-dissolving medicines can reduce the disabilities caused by a
stroke. 
For more information:
American Stroke Association

IF YOU SMOKE OR USE TOBACCO PLEASE READ THE FOLLOWING:
Why is smoking bad for me?
Smoking increases the risk of heart disease, lung disease, vascular disease, stroke, and cancer. If you
smoke, STOP!
For more information:
Quit Now Kentucky
1-800-QUIT-NOW
